Interpreting the Closing Statement of the Logic Text
Bajuri's commentary on the author's closing statement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze the interpretive options for 'tamām' (perfecting vs. all) in the closing phrase and justify the commentator's preferred reading using grammatical and contextual evidence.

Core Idea
The closing phrase is not a boast of completeness but a claim of perfection.

The closing lines of a classical text often carry interpretive significance. The commentator al-Bājūrī unpacks the author's final statement, revealing multiple layers of meaning. This lesson will guide you through his analysis of the phrase 'hādhā tamām al-gharaḍ al-maqṣūd min ummahāt al-manṭiq al-maḥmūd'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the referent of 'hādhā'
Determine what 'this' refers to. The commentator notes two possibilities: the rules just mentioned (the preceding section on errors) or the entire text. The first is more apparent.
2
Analyze the two meanings of 'tamām'
Consider the two interpretations: as 'perfecting' (mutammim) meaning the work completes the rules, or as 'all' (jamī‘) meaning the work contains all the principles. The commentator prefers 'perfecting' as it avoids exaggeration.
The second interpretation is considered far-fetched.
3
Examine the commentator's reasoning for 'gharaḍ'
The commentator explains 'al-gharaḍ' as 'the possessor of purpose' (dhū al-gharaḍ), arguing that the composition itself is not a purpose but has a purpose—divine pleasure and acceptance. He questions the need to claim ellipsis.
This shows attention to the precise meaning of every word.
4
Parse the grammatical possibilities of 'min ummahāt al-manṭiq'
Identify the four combinations: 'min' as explicative or partitive, and the construct as explicative or partitive. Each combination yields a different meaning, e.g., 'from the mothers of logic' as explicative-declarative or partitive.
The commentator notes that even if both are explicative, the claim that the work contains all principles is an exaggeration.
5
Understand the qualifier 'al-maḥmūd'
Recognize that 'praiseworthy' logic excludes logic mixed with philosophical errors. This shows the author's intent to write on logic in accordance with Islamic teachings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۲۸) هَذَا تَمَامُ الغَرَضِ المَقْصُودِ مِنْ أُمَّهَاتِ المَنْطِقِ المَحْمُودِ قَوْلُهُ: (هَذَا تَمَامُ ... إلخ) المُتَبَادَرُ أَنَّ اسْمَ الإِشَارَةِ عَائِدٌ لِمَا تَضَمَّنَهُ قَوْلُهُ: «وَخَطَا البُرْهَانِ... إلخ» مِنَ القَوَاعِدِ، وَعَلَيْهِ فَـ «تَمَامُ) بِمَعْنَى: مُتَمِّم وَجَوَّزَ بَعْضُ المُحَقِّقِينَ أَنَّهُ عَائِدٌ لِمَا تَضَمَّنَهُ كَلَامُهُ فِي هَذَا المَتْنِ مِنَ المَسَائِلِ، وَعَلَيْهِ فَـ «تَمَامُ) يمَعْنَى: جَمِيعِ، وَفِيهِ بُعْدٌ لَا يَخْفَى . وَقَوْلُهُ: (الغَرَضِ) أَيْ: ذِي الغَرَضِ؛ لِأَنَّ هَذَا المُؤَلَّفَ لَيْسَ غَرَضاً لِشَيْءٍ آخَرَ، بَلْ هُوَ ذُو غَرَضِ؛ بِمَعْنَى: أَنَّهُ حَاصِلٌ عَلَيْهِ، وَذَلِكَ الغَرَضُ هُوَ الرّضَا مَعَ القَبُولِ، كَذَا قَالُوا . وَالظَّاهِرُ أَنَّهُ لَا حَاجَةَ لِادِّعَاءِ الحَذْفِ؛ لِأَنَّهُ لَا شَلَّ أَنَّ مَا تَضَمَّنَهُ كَلَامُهُ مِنَ القَوَاعِدِ غَرَضٌ مِنَ التَّألِيفِ، فَلْيُتَأَمَّلْ. قَوْلُهُ: (المَقْصُودِ) صِفَةٌ كَاشِفَةٌ؛ لِأَنَّ الغَرَضَ لَا يَكُونُ إِلَّا مَقْصُوداً . قَوْلُهُ: (مِنْ أُمَّهَاتِ المَنْطِقِ) «مِنَ»: إِمَّا بَيَانِيَّةٌ، أَوْ تَبْعِيضِيَّةٌ، وَالإِضَافَةُ: إِمَّا بَيَانِيَّةٌ، أَوْ تَبْعِيضِيَّةٌ؛ فَتَحَصَّل مِنْ ذَلِكَ الاحْتِمَالَاتُ الأَرْبَعَةُ الَّتي تَقَدَّمَتْ. وَالأُمَّهَاتُ جَمْعُ: «أُمِّ) أَوْ أُمَّهَةٍ عَلَى الخِلَافِ فِي ذَلِكَ، وَالمُرَادُ مِنْهَا هُنَا: الأُصُولُ الَّتِي هِيَ القَوَاعِدُ، وَلَا يَرِدُ عَلَى جَعْلِهِمَا بَيَانِيَّتَيْنِ: أَنَّ هَذَا المُؤَلَّفَ لَيْسَ فِيهِ جَمِيعُ أُمَّهَاتِ المَنْطِقِ؛ لِمَا تَقَدَّمَ مِنْ أَنَّ ذَلِكَ عَلَى سَبِيلِ الادْعَاءِ وَالمُبَالَغَةِ . قَوْلُهُ: (المَحْمُودِ احْتَرَزَ بِهَذَا الوَصْفِ عَنِ المَنْطِقِ غَيْرِ المَحْمُودِ، وَهُوَ المَحْشُرُّ بِضَلَالَاتِ الفَلَاسِفَةِ، كَذَا قَالَ بَعْضُهُمْ.
(128) This is the complete purpose intended from the mothers of praiseworthy logic. His statement: (this is the complete...) The apparent meaning is that the demonstrative pronoun refers to what his statement 'and the error of demonstration...' includes of the rules, and accordingly 'perfect' means perfecting. Some researchers allowed that it refers to what his speech in this text includes of the issues, and accordingly 'perfect' means all, and in it is a distance that is not hidden. His statement: (the purpose) i.e., the possessor of purpose, because this composition is not a purpose for something else, but rather it is possessor of purpose, meaning that it is attained, and that purpose is pleasure with acceptance, as they said. And the apparent is that there is no need to claim deletion, because there is no doubt that what his speech includes of the rules is a purpose of the composition, so let it be considered. His statement: (the intended) is an explicative description, because purpose is not except intended. His statement: (from the mothers of logic) 'min' is either explicative or partitive, and the construct is either explicative or partitive; so are derived the four possibilities that preceded. 'Al-ummahāt' is plural of 'umm' or 'ummaha' depending on the difference, and what is intended by them here are the principles which are the rules. There is no objection to making both explicative that this composition does not contain all the mothers of logic because what preceded that is on the way of claim and exaggeration. His statement: (the praiseworthy) he guarded by this description against logic that is not praiseworthy, which is mixed with the errors of the philosophers, as some of them said.
Source pages p. 352

Commentary
This passage is the concluding remark of the book, where the commentator (Bajuri) explains the author's closing statement. He first discusses what 'this' refers to: either the rules just mentioned (the preceding section on errors) or the entire book. The word 'tamām' is interpreted either as 'perfecting' (i.e., this completes the rules) or 'all' (i.e., all of the mothers of logic). The commentator prefers the first interpretation. Then he explains 'al-gharaḍ' (purpose): the composition itself is not a purpose but has a purpose, which is divine pleasure and acceptance. He argues against claiming an ellipsis. Next, he analyzes 'min ummahāt al-manṭiq' grammatically: 'min' and the construct can be either explicative or partitive, yielding four possible meanings. 'Ummahāt' means the fundamental principles. He notes that even if both are explicative, the claim that this book contains all the principles is an exaggeration. Finally, 'al-maḥmūd' (praiseworthy) distinguishes this logic from blameworthy logic mixed with philosophical errors. This shows the author's intent to write on logic in accordance with Islamic teachings.

Key Terms
تَمَام
الغَرَض
أُمَّهَاتِ المَنْطِق
المَنْطِقِ المَحْمُود

Checkpoint
What is the commentator's preferred interpretation of 'tamām' in the closing phrase?
A) It means 'all' (jamī‘), referring to the entire text.
B) It means 'perfecting' (mutammim), referring to the rules just mentioned.
C) It means 'completion' as in the final part of the book.
D) It means 'excellence' as a term of praise.

Key Takeaway
A single closing phrase can bear multiple valid interpretations, and the commentator guides us to the most likely one through grammatical and contextual reasoning.

Commentary on the Concluding Poem: Unpacking Words and Context
Bajuri explains the source and meaning of the final poem added to the matn.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify how al-Bajuri expands a poetic line by explaining its provenance, defining key terms, and analyzing grammatical structures.

Core Idea
Commentary reveals layers of meaning behind every word of the matn.

Al-Bajuri concludes his commentary with an explanation of the final poem, which is not by the original author but by his father. He walks through each part of the verse, clarifying its origin, the meanings of key words like 'praise', 'Lord', and 'dawn', and the grammar of the construction. This lesson shows you how a commentator unpacks a condensed poetic line to extract its full significance.

Guided Path
1
Trace the provenance of the poem
Notice that al-Bajuri first states the verse is by the author's father, recited in a dream. He then explains why it was included: the father commanded it for blessing, and it contains the phrase 'with the praise of the Lord of the Dawn'.
This addresses any objection about redundancy—the poem is not part of the original matn.
2
Analyze the phrase 'bi-hamd'
Al-Bajuri identifies the 'ba' as for accompaniment and defines 'hamd' as 'eulogy with beauty' (al-thana' bi al-jamil). Consider why this definition is standard and how it relates to the context of praising Allah.
He does not discuss logical genus/differentia here; it is a lexical definition.
3
Examine the multiple meanings of 'rabb'
He lists many meanings of 'rabb' from a poetic source, then selects 'Creator' (al-khaliq) as appropriate here. Note how the context of the Quranic chapter al-Falaq (seeking refuge with the Lord of the Dawn) guides this choice.
This reflects the tafsir method of selecting the most fitting meaning from polysemous terms.
4
Distinguish the two meanings of 'falaq'
'Falaq' can mean the split of dawn (daybreak) or a pit in Hell. Al-Bajuri references the tafsir of Surah al-Falaq. Consider why the daybreak meaning fits better with 'Lord of the Dawn' as a refuge from evil.
The less common meaning (pit in Hell) is mentioned but not selected.
5
Parse the grammatical and terminological analysis
Al-Bajuri explains 'ma' in 'ma rumtuhu' as a relative pronoun or described noun, 'min' as explicative or partitive, and the idafa constructions. He then defines 'nazm' as arranging speech in rhyme and meter. Notice how his focus shifts from semantics to grammar to rhetorical definition.
This illustrates the commentator's comprehensive approach: word meaning, grammar, and technical usage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَوْلُهُ : قَدِ انْتَهَى ... إلخ) هَذَا البَيْتُ لِوَالِدِ المُؤَلِّفِ قَالَهُ فِي مَنَامِهِ، وَكَانَ قَدْ أَخْبَرَهُ بِهَذَا المُؤَلَّفِ، فَأَمَرَهُ بِإِدْخَالِهِ فِيهِ، فَأَدْخَلَهُ رَجَاءَ بَرَكَتِهِ . وَإِذَا كَانَ هَذَا البَيْتُ لَيْسَ مِنْ كَلَام المُصَنِّفِ، فَلَا يَتَوَجَّهُ عَلَيْهِ الاعْتِرَاضُ بِأَنَّهُ لَا حَاجَةَ لَهُ بَعْدَ قَوْلِهِ : هَذَا تَمَامُ الغَرَضِ المَقْصُودِ ؛ عَلَى أَنَّهُ قَدْ يُقَالُ : أَتَى بِهِ بَعْدَ ذَلِكَ لِأَجْلِ قَوْلِهِ : بِحَمْدِ رَبِّ الفَلَقِ»، فَتَأمَّل. قَوْلُهُ : (بِحَمْدِ رَبِّ الفَلَقِ) البَاءُ : لِلمُلَابَسَةِ، وَمَعْنَى الحَمْدِه : الثَّنَاءُ بِالجَمِيلِ كَمَا هُوَ مَعْرُوفٌ . وَ(الرَّبُّ» يُطْلَقُ عَلَى مَعَانٍ مَنْظُومَةٍ فِي قَوْلِ بَعْضِهِمْ : [من الطويل] قَرِيبٌ مُحِيطٌ مَالِكٌ وَمُدَبِّرٌ مُرَبِّ كَثِيرُ الخَيْرِ وَالمُولِ لِلنِّعَمُ وَخَالِقُنَا المَعْبُودُ جَابِرُ كَسْرِنَا وَمُصْلِحُنَا وَالصَّاحِبُ الثَّابِتُ القَدَم وَجَامِعُنَا وَالسَّيِّدُ احْفَظْ فَهَذِهِ مَعَانٍ أَتَتْ لِلرَّبِّ فَادْعُ لِمَنْ نَظَمْ وَالمُنَاسِبُ مِنْهَا هُنَا : الخَالِقُ . وَالفَلَقُ» يُطْلَقُ : عَلَى فَلَقِ الصُّبْحِ، وَعَلَى جُبِّ فِي جَهَنَّمَ؛ كَمَا ذَكَرَهُ بَعْضُهُمْ فِي تَفْسِيرِ قَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى: ﴿قُلْ أَعُوذُ بِرَبِّ الْفَلَقِ ﴾ [الفلق : ١]، فَلْيُرَاجَعْ. قَوْلُهُ : (مَا رُمْتُهُ) أَي : الَّذِي أَوْ شَيْءٍ أَرَدْتُهُ وَقَصَدْتُهُ؛ فَـ «مَا : مَوْصُولَةٌ أَوْ مَوْصُوفَةٌ . وَقَوْلُهُ : (مِنْ فَنْ عِلْمٍ المَنْطِقِ مِنْ»: إِمَّا بَيَانِيَّةٌ أَوْ تَبْعِيضِيَّةٌ عَلَى مَا مَرَّ، وَإِضَافَةُ «فَنّ» لِمَا بَعْدَهُ لِلبَيَانِ، وَإِضَافَةُ عِلْم» لـ «المَنْطِقِ مِنْ إِضَافَةِ المُسَمَّى إِلَى الِاسْمِ. قَوْلُهُ : (نَظَمَهُ) يُطْلَقُ «النَّظْمُ فِي الأَصْلِ عَلَى إِدْخَالِ اللَآلِي فِي السِّلْكِ، وَالمُرَادُ مِنْهُ هُنَا : جَمْعُ الكلام عَلَى وَجْهِ التَّقْفِيةِ وَالوَزْنِ.
His statement: (It has ended... etc.) This verse is by the author's father; he said it in his sleep, and he had informed him about this authored work, and he commanded him to include it in it, so he included it hoping for his blessing. And if this verse is not from the speech of the author, then the objection that there is no need for it after his statement: 'This is the completion of the intended purpose' is not directed against him; however, it may be said: he brought it after that for the sake of his statement: 'With the praise of the Lord of the Dawn', so consider. His statement: (With the praise of the Lord of the Dawn) the 'ba' is for accompaniment, and the meaning of 'praise' is eulogy with beauty as is known. And 'Lord' is applied to meanings composed in the statement of some of them: [in the meter tawil] 'Near, encompassing, owner, and manager, nourisher, abundant in good, and granter of blessings, and our creator, worshipped, mender of our break, and our reformer, and the companion steadfast, and our gatherer, and the master – memorize! So these are meanings that came for 'Lord', so pray for the one who composed them.' And the appropriate among them here is: the Creator. And 'Dawn' is applied to: the split of dawn, and to a pit in Hell; as some of them mentioned in the exegesis of His statement: 'Say: I seek refuge with the Lord of the Dawn' (al-Falaq 1), so let it be referred to. His statement: (what I intended) means: that which or something I wanted and aimed for; so 'ma' is a relative pronoun or a described noun. And his statement: (from the art of the science of logic) 'min' is either explicative or partitive as previously, and the idafa of 'art' to what follows it is for clarification, and the idafa of 'science' to 'logic' is the addition of the named to the name. His statement: (he composed it) 'al-nazm' originally is applied to inserting pearls into the string, and what is meant here is: gathering speech in a rhymed and metered manner.
Source pages p. 353

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the final poem (bayt) that concludes the matn. The commentator, al-Bajuri, first explains the provenance of the poem: it is not by the author of the matn but by his father, who recited it in a dream after being informed about the work. The father commanded its inclusion, and the author included it hoping for blessing. This clarifies why there is no redundancy with the preceding phrase 'This is the completion of the intended purpose'—the poem was added for the sake of the phrase 'with the praise of the Lord of the Dawn' (بِحَمْدِ رَبِّ الْفَلَقِ). The commentator then breaks down the words of the poem. He explains that the 'ba' in 'bi-hamd' is for accompaniment (al-mulabasa), and 'hamd' means eulogy with beauty. He provides a detailed analysis of 'Lord' (rabb), citing a poetic composition that lists its various meanings: near, encompassing, owner, manager, nourisher, granter of blessings, creator, worshipped, mender, reformer, steadfast companion, gatherer, master. From these, he selects 'Creator' (al-khāliq) as the appropriate meaning in this context. For 'Dawn' (al-falaq), he notes two meanings: the split of dawn (i.e., daybreak) and a pit in Hell, referencing the Quranic chapter al-Falaq. He then explains 'what I intended' (mā rumtuhu): 'mā' is either a relative pronoun or a described noun, meaning 'that which' or 'something I intended'. Finally, he analyzes 'from the art of the science of logic' (min fann ʿilm al-manṭiq), noting the particle 'min' and the idafa constructions, similar to previous discussions. He defines 'nazamahu' (he composed it) as originally meaning threading pearls, and here it means arranging speech into rhyme and meter.

Key Terms
الحمد
الرب
الفلق
النظم

A) To provide a summary of the entire work.

C) To complete the number of verses required.
D) To show the author's poetic skill.

Key Takeaway
A commentator expands a condensed poetic line by tracing its origin, defining each word, selecting the appropriate meaning, and parsing the grammar, all to reveal the full intent of the text.

The Honor of Being a Servant: Understanding 'Abd
Author explains the meaning of 'abd and other terms in the poem's invocation and identifies the poet.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the term 'abd (servant) is considered the noblest human attribute in the Islamic tradition, citing textual evidence from the Qur'an and the Prophet's biography.

Core Idea
To be a servant of God is the highest human honor.

The poem begins with the poet calling himself 'al-'abd' (the servant). Al-Bajuri seizes this to deliver a profound lesson: this is not a term of degradation but the loftiest description a human can have. Let's explore why.

Guided Path
1
Locate the definition of 'abd
Find how al-Bajuri defines 'abd: 'the one characterized by utmost humility and submission.'
2
Identify the reasons for its nobility
Notice the two reasons given: it indicates God's perfection and human need, and it points to complete submission to the Master.
3
Examine the Qur'anic evidence
Al-Bajuri cites three verses where the Prophet is called 'abd: in the Night Journey (Isra 17:1), revelation of the Book (Kahf 18:1), and calling upon God (Jinn 72:19). Understand how each context elevates the term.
4
Understand the Prophet's choice
The Prophet was offered to be a prophet-king or a prophet-servant; he chose the latter. This shows the superiority of servitude to God over worldly power.
Reflect on the verse and the poetic quote from Qadi 'Iyad.

وَقَوْلُهُ : (العَبْدُ) أي: المُتَّصِفُ بِالعُبُودِيَّةِ الَّتِي هِيَ غَايَةُ الخُضُوع وَالتَّذَلُّلِ، وَهَذَا الوَصْفُ أَشْرَفُ أَوْصَافِ الإِنْسَانِ وَأَرْفَعُهَا ؛ لِمَا فِيهِ مِنَ الإِشَارَةِ إِلَى كَمَالِ اللهِ تَعَالَى وَاحْتِيَاجُ غَيْرِهِ إِلَيْهِ لِدَلَالَتِهِ عَلَى كَمَالِ الخُضُوعِ وَالتَّذَلُّلِ لِلمَوْلَى تَبَارَكَ وَتَعَالَى، وَلِذَا وُصِفَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم بِهِ يَكُونَ نَبِيًّا مَلِكَاً وَأَنْ يَكُونَ نَبِيًّا عَبْداً، فَاخْتَارَ الثَّانِي، وَمِمَّا يُنْسَبُ لِلقَاضِي عِيَاضٍ : [من الوافر] وَمِمَّا زَادَنِي شَرَفاً وَتِـيـهــا وَكِدْتُ بِأَخْمَصِي أَطَا الثريا دُخُولِي تَحْتَ قَوْلِكَ : يَعِبَادِي وَأَنْ صَيَّرْتَ أَحْمَدَ لِي نَبِيًّا قَوْلُهُ : (الذَّلِيْلُ) تَأكِيدٌ لِمَا يُفْهَمُ مِنَ العَبْدِ». قَوْلُهُ : (المُفْتَقِرْ) هُوَ أَبْلَغُ مِنَ الفَقِيرِ ) ؛ لِأَنَّ مَعْنَى المُفْتَقِرِ : شَدِيدُ الاحْتِيَاجِ، وَمَعْنَى الفَقِيرِ» المُحْتَاجُ ، لا لأَنَّ بِنَاءَ المُفْتَقِرِ» زَائِدٌ عَلَى بِنَاءِ الفَقِيرِ»؛ لِأَنَّ مَحَلَّ قَوْلِهِمْ: زِيَادَةُ البِنَاءِ تَدُلُّ عَلَى زِيَادَةِ المَعْنَى إِذَا اتَّحَدَ نَوْعُ الكَلِمَتَيْنِ ؛ كَأَنْ يَكُونَا اسْمَيْ فَاعِلٍ، أَوْ صِفَةٌ مُشَبَّهَةٌ، وَمَا هُنَا لَيْسَ كَذَلِكَ ؛ لِأَنَّ المُفْتَقِرَ اسْمُ فَاعِلِ يَدُلُّ عَلَى الحُدُوثِ ، وَالفَقِيرَ صِفَةٌ مُشَبَّهَةٌ تَدُلُّ عَلَى الدَّوَامِ . نَعَمْ يُمْكِنُ أَنْ يُجْعَلَ المُفْتَقِرُ) صِفَةٌ مُشَبَّهَةٌ بِأَنْ يُرَادَ مِنْهُ الدَّوَامَ . . قَوْلُهُ : (لِرَحْمَةِ المَوْلَى أَيْ : لإِحْسَانِهِ أَوْ لِإِرَادَتِهِ ؛ لِأَنَّهُ لَا يَصِحُ إِرَادَةُ المَعْنَى الأَصْلِي فِي حَقِّهِ تَعَالَى، وَهُوَ : «الرِّقَةُ» ؛ لِاسْتِحَالَتِهِ عَلَيْهِ تَعَالَى، وَإِذَا اسْتَحَالَ إِطْلَاقُهَا فِي حَقِّهِ تَعَالَى بِاعْتِبَارِ مَبْدَئِهَا ، جَازَ إِطْلَاقُهَا فِي حَقِّهِ تَعَالَى بِاعْتِبَارِ غَايَتِهَا وَهِيَ الإِحْسَانِ، أَوْ إِرَادَتِهِ؛ وَهِيَ عَلَى الْأَوَّلِ : صِفَةُ فِعْلٍ، وَعَلَى الثَّانِي : صِفَةُ ذَاتٍ . وَ المَوْلَى يُطْلَقُ عَلَى مَعَانٍ كَثِيرَةٍ مِنْهَا : الحَلِيفُ ، وَالنَّاصِرُ ، وَالحَلِيمُ الَّذِي لَا يَسْتَفِرُّهُ الغَضَبُ . قَوْلُهُ : (العَظِيْمِ) أَيْ : عَظَمَةٌ مَعْنَوِيَّةٌ، لَا حِرِّيَّةٌ؛ لِاسْتِحَالَتِهِ عَلَيْهِ تَعَالَى، فَإِنَّهَا تَسْتَدْعِي الجِسْمِيَّةَ. قَوْلُهُ : (المُقْتَدِرْ) هُوَ أَبْلَغُ مِنَ القَادِرِ » ؛ لِأَنَّ مَعْنَى المُقْتَدِرِ »: تَامُ القُدْرَةِ، وَمَعْنَى القَادِرِ» : المُتَّصِفُ بِالقُدْرَةِ، وَيَصِحُ هُنَا أَنْ يُقَالَ : لِأَنَّ زِيَادَةَ البِنَاءِ تَدُلُّ عَلَى زِيَادَةِ المَعْنَى؛ لاتِّحَادِ نَوْعِ الكَلِمَتَيْنِ المَذْكُورَتَيْنِ، فَإِنَّهُمَا اسْمَا فَاعِلِ. قَوْلُهُ : (الأَخْضَرِيُّ) نِسْبَةٌ لِـ «الأَخْضَر جَبَلْ بِالمَغْرِبِ عَلَى مَا قَالَهُ بَعْضُ المَغَارِبَةِ. وَهَذَا بَيَانُ لِنِسْبَتِهِ بِحَسَبِ مَا اشْتُهِرَ عَلَى الأَلْسِنَةِ، وَإِلَّا فَهُوَ مَنْسُوبٌ لِلعَبَّاسِ بْنِ مِرْدَاسَ الصَّحَابِيِّ المَشْهُورِ، كَمَا قَالَهُ المُصَنِّفُ فِي شَرْحِهِ. قَوْلُهُ : (عَابِدُ الرَّحْمَنِ) إِنَّمَا زَادَ الأَلِفَ فِي ذَلِكَ لِلوَزْنِ، وَإِلَّا فَاسْمُهُ: «عَبْدُ الرَّحْمَنِ»، وَيُحْتَمَلُ أَنَّ المُصَنِّفَ لَمْ يُرِدِ العَلَمَ . قَوْلُهُ : (المُرْتَجِيْ أَي : المُؤَمِّلَ مَعَ الأَخْذِ فِي الأَسْبَابِ كَمَا يُعْلَمُ مِمَّا مَرَّ، وَمَعْمُولُ قَوْلِهِ : المُرْتَجِيْ مَا ذَكَرَهُ بِقَوْلِهِ : «مَغْفِرَةٌ تُحِيطُ ... إلخ » ، وَقَوْلِهِ : وَإِنْ يُبَنَا ... إلخ». قَوْلُهُ : ( مِنْ رَبِّهِ المَنَّانِ) أَيْ : كَثِيرِ المَنِّ ؛ الَّذِي هُوَ الإِنْعَامِ، أَوْ تَعْدَادُ النِّعَمِ ، وَهُوَ بِالمَعْنَى الثَّانِي مَذْمُومٌ ؛ إِلَّا بِالنِّسْبَةِ اللهِ وَرَسُولِهِ ، وَاسْتَتَنى بَعْضُهُمُ الشَّيْخَ وَالوَالِدَ . قَوْلُهُ : (مَغْفِرَةٌ) مَأخوذَةٌ مِنَ الغَفْرِ (۳) وَهُوَ : السِّتْرُ، وَالمُرَادُ بِهَا : سِتْرُ الذُّنُوبِ عَنْ أَعْيُنِ المَلَائِكَةِ قِيلَ : مَعَ كَوْنِهَا بَاقِيَةٌ فِي الصَّحِيفَةِ، لَكِنْ لَا يُؤَاخِذُ بِهَا صَاحِبُهَا، وَقِيلَ: مَعَ مَحْوِهَا مِنَ الصَّحِيفَةِ مِنْ أَصْلِهَا . قَوْلُهُ : (تُحِيْطُ بالذُّنُوبِ كِنَايَةٌ عَنْ كَوْنِهَا تَعُمُّ جَمِيعَهَا بِحَيْثُ لَا يَبْقَى فَرْدٌ مِنْهَا .
And his statement (the servant): meaning the one characterized by servitude which is the utmost humility and submission, and this description is the noblest and highest of human descriptions because of what it contains of indication of the perfection of God Most High and the need of others for Him due to its indication of complete humility and submission to the Master, blessed and exalted. For this reason, the Messenger of God, may God bless him and grant him peace, was described with it in the highest stations: like the station of the Night Journey, the station of the revelation of the Qur'an, and the station of calling to Him. God Most High said: 'Exalted is He who took His servant by night' [Al-Isra: 1], 'Praise be to God who sent down upon His servant the Book' [Al-Kahf: 1], 'And that when the servant of God stood calling upon Him' [Al-Jinn: 19], and others. Then he, peace be upon him, was given the choice between being a prophet-king and a prophet-servant, and he chose the second. And among what is attributed to Qadi 'Iyad: [in the meter al-wafir]: 'And what increased my honor and pride, so that I almost step on the Pleiades with the sole of my foot, is my entering under Your saying: O My servants, and that You made Ahmad a prophet for me.' His statement (the lowly) is a confirmation of what is understood from 'the servant.' His statement (the in need) is more intensive than 'the poor' because the meaning of 'al-muftaqir' is intensely needy, and the meaning of 'al-faqir' is needy, not because the pattern of 'al-muftaqir' is longer than the pattern of 'al-faqir', because the place of their saying 'increase in pattern indicates increase in meaning' is when the type of the two words is the same, like both being active participles or descriptive adjectives, and here it is not so, because 'al-muftaqir' is an active participle indicating temporality, and 'al-faqir' is a descriptive adjective indicating permanence. Yes, it is possible to make 'al-muftaqir' a descriptive adjective by intending from it permanence. His statement (for the mercy of the Master) meaning: for His beneficence or for His will, because it is not valid to intend the original meaning with respect to Him Most High, which is 'tenderness' because of its impossibility upon Him Most High. And when it is impossible to apply it to Him Most High in terms of its origin, it is permissible to apply it to Him Most High in terms of its outcome, which is beneficence, or His will. And it is, according to the first, an attribute of action, and according to the second, an attribute of essence. And 'al-mawla' is applied to many meanings, among them: ally, supporter, and the forbearing one whom anger does not arouse. His statement (the Great) meaning: a conceptual greatness, not physical, because of its impossibility upon Him Most High, for it entails corporeality. His statement (the Powerful) is more intensive than 'the powerful one', because the meaning of 'al-muqtadir' is perfect in power, and the meaning of 'al-qadir' is the one described with power. And it is valid here to say: because increase in pattern indicates increase in meaning, because the type of the two mentioned words is the same, for they are both active participles. His statement (al-Akhdari) is a relative attribution to 'al-Akhdar', a mountain in the Maghreb according to what some Maghrebis said. And this is an explanation of his lineage according to what is commonly known by tongues; otherwise, he is attributed to al-'Abbas ibn Mirdas, the famous companion, as the author said in his commentary. His statement (worshipper of al-Rahman) He added the alif only for the meter; otherwise his name is 'Abd al-Rahman, and it is possible that the author did not intend the proper noun. His statement (the one who hopes) meaning: the one who expects while taking the means, as is known from what has passed. And the object of his statement 'the one who hopes' is what he mentioned by his statement 'a forgiveness that encompasses... etc.' and his statement 'and if we are built... etc.' His statement (from His Lord, the Bestower) meaning: abundant in bestowal, which is granting favors, or counting favors. And it is, in the second sense, blameworthy except with respect to God and His Messenger, and some excluded the teacher and the father. His statement (forgiveness) is derived from 'al-ghafr' which is concealment, and what is intended by it is the concealment of sins from the eyes of the angels. It is said: while they remain in the record, but their owner is not taken to task for them; and it is said: with their erasure from the record entirely. His statement (encompasses the sins) is a metaphor for it encompassing all of them such that no individual sin remains.
Source pages p. 354

Commentary
This passage is a commentary by al-Bajuri on the opening lines of the poem 'al-Sullam al-Murawnaq' by al-Akhdari. The author explains the meaning of the poet's self-description as 'the servant, the lowly, the in need of the mercy of the Master, the Great, the Powerful.' He begins by extolling the description 'servant' ('abd), stating it is the noblest human attribute because it acknowledges God's perfection and human need. He supports this with Qur'anic verses where the Prophet is called 'abd in the Night Journey, the revelation of the Qur'an, and his call. He then mentions that the Prophet chose to be a prophet-servant over a prophet-king, and cites a poetic line by Qadi 'Iyad about the honor of being a servant. Next, he clarifies that 'al-dhalil' (lowly) reinforces the meaning of 'abd. He then distinguishes between 'al-muftaqir' and 'al-faqir', noting that 'muftaqir' is more intense and temporally rooted, while 'faqir' is a permanent state. He adds that it is possible to interpret 'muftaqir' as permanent if desired. Then he explains 'rahmat al-mawla' as either God's beneficence (an attribute of action) or His will (an attribute of essence), since 'mercy' in its literal sense of tenderness cannot apply to God. He lists some meanings of 'mawla': ally, supporter, forbearing. He then notes that 'al-'azim' (the Great) refers to conceptual, not physical, greatness, and that 'al-muqtadir' (the Powerful) is more intensive than 'al-qadir' because of the increased pattern and both are active participles. After explaining these divine attributes, he turns to the poet's name. He states that 'al-Akhdari' is an attribution to a mountain called al-Akhdar in the Maghreb, but actually the poet traces his lineage to al-'Abbas ibn Mirdas, a famous Companion, as the author himself mentioned in his commentary. He then notes that the poet's name 'Abid al-Rahman' is actually 'Abd al-Rahman' but the alif was added for meter; it may not be a proper noun. He explains 'al-murtaiji' as one who hopes while taking means. He then clarifies 'al-Mannan' (the Bestower) as abundant in giving favors, but warns that counting favors is blameworthy except by God and His Messenger (and, some say, by a teacher or parent). Finally, he defines 'maghfirah' (forgiveness) as concealment of sins from angels, with two opinions: sins remain but are not punished, or they are erased entirely. And 'tuhitu bi al-dhunub' (encompasses sins) is a metaphor for complete coverage, leaving no sin unencompassed.

Checkpoint
According to al-Bajuri's commentary, why is the description 'abd' (servant) considered the noblest human attribute?
A) Because it signals wealth and power.
B) Because it indicates complete humility and need of God, and the Prophet was described with it.
C) Because it is a poetic term used for rhythm.
D) Because it means freedom from sin.

Key Takeaway
The term 'abd, far from being degrading, is the highest honor for humans, especially the Prophet, because it signifies complete devotion and need for God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Using al-Bajuri's reasoning, explain why the Prophet's choice of being a prophet-servant over a prophet-king demonstrates the superiority of 'abd. Write two sentences.

Commentary Notes
intermediate
5 min
Lexical Nuances: Increase in Pattern and Meaning
Author explains the meaning of 'abd and other terms in the poem's invocation and identifies the poet.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the principle 'increase in pattern indicates increase in meaning' to distinguish between intensive and non-intensive forms in Arabic, using examples from the commentary.

Core Idea
Not all longer Arabic words carry stronger meaning; the grammatical type must match.

Al-Bajuri delves into a grammatical rule: sometimes a longer word form implies a more intense meaning, but not always. He contrasts muftaqir/faqir and muqtadir/qadir to illustrate when the rule applies and when it doesn't.

Guided Path
1
Compare muftaqir and faqir
Note that muftaqir means 'intensely needy' while faqir means 'needy'. Despite muftaqir being longer, al-Bajuri says the increase in pattern does not automatically indicate increase in meaning because they are different grammatical types.
muftaqir is an active participle (temporary), faqir is a descriptive adjective (permanent).
2
Identify the rule and its condition
The rule 'increase in pattern indicates increase in meaning' applies only when both words are of the same type (e.g., both active participles or both descriptive adjectives).
3
Apply to muqtadir and qadir
In contrast, muqtadir and qadir are both active participles. Thus the increase in pattern (muqtadir has more letters) does indicate increase in meaning: muqtadir is 'perfect in power' while qadir is just 'one described with power'.
Al-Bajuri explicitly validates this application.
4
Consider the exception
Al-Bajuri notes that one can treat muftaqir as a descriptive adjective (by intending permanence), which would then allow the rule to apply. This shows the flexibility of Arabic morphology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَقَوْلُهُ : (العَبْدُ) أي: المُتَّصِفُ بِالعُبُودِيَّةِ الَّتِي هِيَ غَايَةُ الخُضُوع وَالتَّذَلُّلِ، وَهَذَا الوَصْفُ أَشْرَفُ أَوْصَافِ الإِنْسَانِ وَأَرْفَعُهَا ؛ لِمَا فِيهِ مِنَ الإِشَارَةِ إِلَى كَمَالِ اللهِ تَعَالَى وَاحْتِيَاجُ غَيْرِهِ إِلَيْهِ لِدَلَالَتِهِ عَلَى كَمَالِ الخُضُوعِ وَالتَّذَلُّلِ لِلمَوْلَى تَبَارَكَ وَتَعَالَى، وَلِذَا وُصِفَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم بِهِ فِي المَقَامَاتِ العُلْيَّةِ ك: مَقَامِ الإِسْرَاءِ، وَمَقَامِ إِنْزَالِ القُرْآنِ، وَمَقَامِ الدَّعْوَةِ إِلَيْهِ؛ قَالَ تَعَالَى : وسُبْحَانَ الَّذِي أَسْرَى بِعَبْدِهِ [الإسراء : ( الْحَمدُ لِلهِ الَّذِي أَنزَلَ عَلَى عَبْدِهِ الكتب الله [الكهف : ١]، ﴿ وَأَنَّهُ لَمَّا قَامَ عَبْدُ اللَّهِ يَدْعُوهُ ﴾ [الجن: ١٩] ١]، إِلَى غَيْرِ ذَلِكَ، وَمِنْ ثُمَّ خُيِّرَ صلى الله عليه وسلم بَيْنَ أَنْ يَكُونَ نَبِيًّا مَلِكَاً وَأَنْ يَكُونَ نَبِيًّا عَبْداً، فَاخْتَارَ الثَّانِي، وَمِمَّا يُنْسَبُ لِلقَاضِي عِيَاضٍ : [من الوافر] وَمِمَّا زَادَنِي شَرَفاً وَتِـيـهــا وَكِدْتُ بِأَخْمَصِي أَطَا الثريا دُخُولِي تَحْتَ قَوْلِكَ : يَعِبَادِي وَأَنْ صَيَّرْتَ أَحْمَدَ لِي نَبِيًّا قَوْلُهُ : (الذَّلِيْلُ) تَأكِيدٌ لِمَا يُفْهَمُ مِنَ العَبْدِ». قَوْلُهُ : (المُفْتَقِرْ) هُوَ أَبْلَغُ مِنَ الفَقِيرِ ) ؛ لِأَنَّ مَعْنَى المُفْتَقِرِ : شَدِيدُ الاحْتِيَاجِ، وَمَعْنَى الفَقِيرِ» المُحْتَاجُ ، لا لأَنَّ بِنَاءَ المُفْتَقِرِ» زَائِدٌ عَلَى بِنَاءِ الفَقِيرِ»؛ لِأَنَّ مَحَلَّ قَوْلِهِمْ: زِيَادَةُ البِنَاءِ تَدُلُّ عَلَى زِيَادَةِ المَعْنَى إِذَا اتَّحَدَ نَوْعُ الكَلِمَتَيْنِ ؛ كَأَنْ يَكُونَا اسْمَيْ فَاعِلٍ، أَوْ صِفَةٌ مُشَبَّهَةٌ، وَمَا هُنَا لَيْسَ كَذَلِكَ ؛ لِأَنَّ المُفْتَقِرَ اسْمُ فَاعِلِ يَدُلُّ عَلَى الحُدُوثِ ، وَالفَقِيرَ صِفَةٌ مُشَبَّهَةٌ تَدُلُّ عَلَى الدَّوَامِ . نَعَمْ يُمْكِنُ أَنْ يُجْعَلَ المُفْتَقِرُ) صِفَةٌ مُشَبَّهَةٌ بِأَنْ يُرَادَ مِنْهُ الدَّوَامَ . . قَوْلُهُ : (لِرَحْمَةِ المَوْلَى أَيْ : لإِحْسَانِهِ أَوْ لِإِرَادَتِهِ ؛ لِأَنَّهُ لَا يَصِحُ إِرَادَةُ المَعْنَى الأَصْلِي فِي حَقِّهِ تَعَالَى، وَهُوَ : «الرِّقَةُ» ؛ لِاسْتِحَالَتِهِ عَلَيْهِ تَعَالَى، وَإِذَا اسْتَحَالَ إِطْلَاقُهَا فِي حَقِّهِ تَعَالَى بِاعْتِبَارِ مَبْدَئِهَا ، جَازَ إِطْلَاقُهَا فِي حَقِّهِ تَعَالَى بِاعْتِبَارِ غَايَتِهَا وَهِيَ الإِحْسَانِ، أَوْ إِرَادَتِهِ؛ وَهِيَ عَلَى الْأَوَّلِ : صِفَةُ فِعْلٍ، وَعَلَى الثَّانِي : صِفَةُ ذَاتٍ . وَ المَوْلَى يُطْلَقُ عَلَى مَعَانٍ كَثِيرَةٍ مِنْهَا : الحَلِيفُ ، وَالنَّاصِرُ ، وَالحَلِيمُ الَّذِي لَا يَسْتَفِرُّهُ الغَضَبُ . قَوْلُهُ : (العَظِيْمِ) أَيْ : عَظَمَةٌ مَعْنَوِيَّةٌ، لَا حِرِّيَّةٌ؛ لِاسْتِحَالَتِهِ عَلَيْهِ تَعَالَى، فَإِنَّهَا تَسْتَدْعِي الجِسْمِيَّةَ. قَوْلُهُ : (المُقْتَدِرْ) هُوَ أَبْلَغُ مِنَ القَادِرِ » ؛ لِأَنَّ مَعْنَى المُقْتَدِرِ »: تَامُ القُدْرَةِ، وَمَعْنَى القَادِرِ» : المُتَّصِفُ بِالقُدْرَةِ، وَيَصِحُ هُنَا أَنْ يُقَالَ : لِأَنَّ زِيَادَةَ البِنَاءِ تَدُلُّ عَلَى زِيَادَةِ المَعْنَى؛ لاتِّحَادِ نَوْعِ الكَلِمَتَيْنِ المَذْكُورَتَيْنِ، فَإِنَّهُمَا اسْمَا فَاعِلِ. قَوْلُهُ : (الأَخْضَرِيُّ) نِسْبَةٌ لِـ «الأَخْضَر جَبَلْ بِالمَغْرِبِ عَلَى مَا قَالَهُ بَعْضُ المَغَارِبَةِ. وَهَذَا بَيَانُ لِنِسْبَتِهِ بِحَسَبِ مَا اشْتُهِرَ عَلَى الأَلْسِنَةِ، وَإِلَّا فَهُوَ مَنْسُوبٌ لِلعَبَّاسِ بْنِ مِرْدَاسَ الصَّحَابِيِّ المَشْهُورِ، كَمَا قَالَهُ المُصَنِّفُ فِي شَرْحِهِ. قَوْلُهُ : (عَابِدُ الرَّحْمَنِ) إِنَّمَا زَادَ الأَلِفَ فِي ذَلِكَ لِلوَزْنِ، وَإِلَّا فَاسْمُهُ: «عَبْدُ الرَّحْمَنِ»، وَيُحْتَمَلُ أَنَّ المُصَنِّفَ لَمْ يُرِدِ العَلَمَ . قَوْلُهُ : (المُرْتَجِيْ أَي : المُؤَمِّلَ مَعَ الأَخْذِ فِي الأَسْبَابِ كَمَا يُعْلَمُ مِمَّا مَرَّ، وَمَعْمُولُ قَوْلِهِ : المُرْتَجِيْ مَا ذَكَرَهُ بِقَوْلِهِ : «مَغْفِرَةٌ تُحِيطُ ... إلخ » ، وَقَوْلِهِ : وَإِنْ يُبَنَا ... إلخ». قَوْلُهُ : ( مِنْ رَبِّهِ المَنَّانِ) أَيْ : كَثِيرِ المَنِّ ؛ الَّذِي هُوَ الإِنْعَامِ، أَوْ تَعْدَادُ النِّعَمِ ، وَهُوَ بِالمَعْنَى الثَّانِي مَذْمُومٌ ؛ إِلَّا بِالنِّسْبَةِ اللهِ وَرَسُولِهِ ، وَاسْتَتَنى بَعْضُهُمُ الشَّيْخَ وَالوَالِدَ . قَوْلُهُ : (مَغْفِرَةٌ) مَأخوذَةٌ مِنَ الغَفْرِ (۳) وَهُوَ : السِّتْرُ، وَالمُرَادُ بِهَا : سِتْرُ الذُّنُوبِ عَنْ أَعْيُنِ المَلَائِكَةِ قِيلَ : مَعَ كَوْنِهَا بَاقِيَةٌ فِي الصَّحِيفَةِ، لَكِنْ لَا يُؤَاخِذُ بِهَا صَاحِبُهَا، وَقِيلَ: مَعَ مَحْوِهَا مِنَ الصَّحِيفَةِ مِنْ أَصْلِهَا . قَوْلُهُ : (تُحِيْطُ بالذُّنُوبِ كِنَايَةٌ عَنْ كَوْنِهَا تَعُمُّ جَمِيعَهَا بِحَيْثُ لَا يَبْقَى فَرْدٌ مِنْهَا .
And his statement (the servant): meaning the one characterized by servitude which is the utmost humility and submission, and this description is the noblest and highest of human descriptions because of what it contains of indication of the perfection of God Most High and the need of others for Him due to its indication of complete humility and submission to the Master, blessed and exalted. For this reason, the Messenger of God, may God bless him and grant him peace, was described with it in the highest stations: like the station of the Night Journey, the station of the revelation of the Qur'an, and the station of calling to Him. God Most High said: 'Exalted is He who took His servant by night' [Al-Isra: 1], 'Praise be to God who sent down upon His servant the Book' [Al-Kahf: 1], 'And that when the servant of God stood calling upon Him' [Al-Jinn: 19], and others. Then he, peace be upon him, was given the choice between being a prophet-king and a prophet-servant, and he chose the second. And among what is attributed to Qadi 'Iyad: [in the meter al-wafir]: 'And what increased my honor and pride, so that I almost step on the Pleiades with the sole of my foot, is my entering under Your saying: O My servants, and that You made Ahmad a prophet for me.' His statement (the lowly) is a confirmation of what is understood from 'the servant.' His statement (the in need) is more intensive than 'the poor' because the meaning of 'al-muftaqir' is intensely needy, and the meaning of 'al-faqir' is needy, not because the pattern of 'al-muftaqir' is longer than the pattern of 'al-faqir', because the place of their saying 'increase in pattern indicates increase in meaning' is when the type of the two words is the same, like both being active participles or descriptive adjectives, and here it is not so, because 'al-muftaqir' is an active participle indicating temporality, and 'al-faqir' is a descriptive adjective indicating permanence. Yes, it is possible to make 'al-muftaqir' a descriptive adjective by intending from it permanence. His statement (for the mercy of the Master) meaning: for His beneficence or for His will, because it is not valid to intend the original meaning with respect to Him Most High, which is 'tenderness' because of its impossibility upon Him Most High. And when it is impossible to apply it to Him Most High in terms of its origin, it is permissible to apply it to Him Most High in terms of its outcome, which is beneficence, or His will. And it is, according to the first, an attribute of action, and according to the second, an attribute of essence. And 'al-mawla' is applied to many meanings, among them: ally, supporter, and the forbearing one whom anger does not arouse. His statement (the Great) meaning: a conceptual greatness, not physical, because of its impossibility upon Him Most High, for it entails corporeality. His statement (the Powerful) is more intensive than 'the powerful one', because the meaning of 'al-muqtadir' is perfect in power, and the meaning of 'al-qadir' is the one described with power. And it is valid here to say: because increase in pattern indicates increase in meaning, because the type of the two mentioned words is the same, for they are both active participles. His statement (al-Akhdari) is a relative attribution to 'al-Akhdar', a mountain in the Maghreb according to what some Maghrebis said. And this is an explanation of his lineage according to what is commonly known by tongues; otherwise, he is attributed to al-'Abbas ibn Mirdas, the famous companion, as the author said in his commentary. His statement (worshipper of al-Rahman) He added the alif only for the meter; otherwise his name is 'Abd al-Rahman, and it is possible that the author did not intend the proper noun. His statement (the one who hopes) meaning: the one who expects while taking the means, as is known from what has passed. And the object of his statement 'the one who hopes' is what he mentioned by his statement 'a forgiveness that encompasses... etc.' and his statement 'and if we are built... etc.' His statement (from His Lord, the Bestower) meaning: abundant in bestowal, which is granting favors, or counting favors. And it is, in the second sense, blameworthy except with respect to God and His Messenger, and some excluded the teacher and the father. His statement (forgiveness) is derived from 'al-ghafr' which is concealment, and what is intended by it is the concealment of sins from the eyes of the angels. It is said: while they remain in the record, but their owner is not taken to task for them; and it is said: with their erasure from the record entirely. His statement (encompasses the sins) is a metaphor for it encompassing all of them such that no individual sin remains.
Source pages p. 354

Commentary
This passage is a commentary by al-Bajuri on the opening lines of the poem 'al-Sullam al-Murawnaq' by al-Akhdari. The author explains the meaning of the poet's self-description as 'the servant, the lowly, the in need of the mercy of the Master, the Great, the Powerful.' He begins by extolling the description 'servant' ('abd), stating it is the noblest human attribute because it acknowledges God's perfection and human need. He supports this with Qur'anic verses where the Prophet is called 'abd in the Night Journey, the revelation of the Qur'an, and his call. He then mentions that the Prophet chose to be a prophet-servant over a prophet-king, and cites a poetic line by Qadi 'Iyad about the honor of being a servant. Next, he clarifies that 'al-dhalil' (lowly) reinforces the meaning of 'abd. He then distinguishes between 'al-muftaqir' and 'al-faqir', noting that 'muftaqir' is more intense and temporally rooted, while 'faqir' is a permanent state. He adds that it is possible to interpret 'muftaqir' as permanent if desired. Then he explains 'rahmat al-mawla' as either God's beneficence (an attribute of action) or His will (an attribute of essence), since 'mercy' in its literal sense of tenderness cannot apply to God. He lists some meanings of 'mawla': ally, supporter, forbearing. He then notes that 'al-'azim' (the Great) refers to conceptual, not physical, greatness, and that 'al-muqtadir' (the Powerful) is more intensive than 'al-qadir' because of the increased pattern and both are active participles. After explaining these divine attributes, he turns to the poet's name. He states that 'al-Akhdari' is an attribution to a mountain called al-Akhdar in the Maghreb, but actually the poet traces his lineage to al-'Abbas ibn Mirdas, a famous Companion, as the author himself mentioned in his commentary. He then notes that the poet's name 'Abid al-Rahman' is actually 'Abd al-Rahman' but the alif was added for meter; it may not be a proper noun. He explains 'al-murtaiji' as one who hopes while taking means. He then clarifies 'al-Mannan' (the Bestower) as abundant in giving favors, but warns that counting favors is blameworthy except by God and His Messenger (and, some say, by a teacher or parent). Finally, he defines 'maghfirah' (forgiveness) as concealment of sins from angels, with two opinions: sins remain but are not punished, or they are erased entirely. And 'tuhitu bi al-dhunub' (encompasses sins) is a metaphor for complete coverage, leaving no sin unencompassed.

المفتقر
الفقير
المقتدر
القادر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does al-Bajuri say that 'al-muftaqir' is more intensive than 'al-faqir' despite the pattern being longer?
A) Because increase in pattern always indicates increase in meaning.
B) Because 'muftaqir' is an active participle indicating intense need, while 'faqir' is a descriptive adjective indicating simple need.
C) Because 'muftaqir' is a descriptive adjective indicating permanence.
D) Because 'faqir' is not a real word.

Key Takeaway
The rule 'increase in pattern indicates increase in meaning' requires the words to be of the same grammatical type; otherwise, the intensity comes from the specific morphology and meaning.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the Arabic pair 'alim (knowing) and 'allam (very knowing). Are they both active participles? Apply the principle to determine if 'allam is more intensive. Write your reasoning.

Commentary Notes
beginner
5 min
Poet's Lineage and Theology of Forgiveness
Author explains the meaning of 'abd and other terms in the poem's invocation and identifies the poet.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to trace the lineage of al-Akhdari as given in the commentary and explain the theological nuances of al-Mannan and maghfirah.

Core Idea
A poet's lineage and God's attributes require precise exegesis.

Al-Bajuri moves from grammatical analysis to biography and theology. He corrects a common misconception about the poet's lineage and explains two important divine attributes: al-Mannan (the Bestower) and maghfirah (forgiveness).

Guided Path
1
Identify the apparent attribution
The poet is called al-Akhdari, which seems to attribute him to a mountain called al-Akhdar in the Maghreb.
2
Note the correction
Al-Bajuri says the real lineage is to al-'Abbas ibn Mirdas, a Companion, as stated by the author of the commentary (al-Bannani).
3
Understand al-Mannan's two meanings
Al-Mannan can mean 'abundant in bestowal' (praiseworthy) or 'one who counts favors' (blameworthy except for God and His Messenger). The second sense is blameworthy for humans.
Some scholars also exclude teacher and father.
4
Define maghfirah
Maghfirah is derived from 'concealment' and here means concealment of sins from angels. There are two opinions: sins remain in the record but are not punished, or sins are erased entirely.
The phrase 'encompasses the sins' is a metaphor for complete coverage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَقَوْلُهُ : (العَبْدُ) أي: المُتَّصِفُ بِالعُبُودِيَّةِ الَّتِي هِيَ غَايَةُ الخُضُوع وَالتَّذَلُّلِ، وَهَذَا الوَصْفُ أَشْرَفُ أَوْصَافِ الإِنْسَانِ وَأَرْفَعُهَا ؛ لِمَا فِيهِ مِنَ الإِشَارَةِ إِلَى كَمَالِ اللهِ تَعَالَى وَاحْتِيَاجُ غَيْرِهِ إِلَيْهِ لِدَلَالَتِهِ عَلَى كَمَالِ الخُضُوعِ وَالتَّذَلُّلِ لِلمَوْلَى تَبَارَكَ وَتَعَالَى، وَلِذَا وُصِفَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم بِهِ فِي المَقَامَاتِ العُلْيَّةِ ك: مَقَامِ الإِسْرَاءِ، وَمَقَامِ إِنْزَالِ القُرْآنِ، وَمَقَامِ الدَّعْوَةِ إِلَيْهِ؛ قَالَ تَعَالَى : وسُبْحَانَ الَّذِي أَسْرَى بِعَبْدِهِ [الإسراء : ( الْحَمدُ لِلهِ الَّذِي أَنزَلَ عَلَى عَبْدِهِ الكتب الله [الكهف : ١]، ﴿ وَأَنَّهُ لَمَّا قَامَ عَبْدُ اللَّهِ يَدْعُوهُ ﴾ [الجن: ١٩] ١]، إِلَى غَيْرِ ذَلِكَ، وَمِنْ ثُمَّ خُيِّرَ صلى الله عليه وسلم بَيْنَ أَنْ يَكُونَ نَبِيًّا مَلِكَاً وَأَنْ يَكُونَ نَبِيًّا عَبْداً، فَاخْتَارَ الثَّانِي، وَمِمَّا يُنْسَبُ لِلقَاضِي عِيَاضٍ : [من الوافر] وَمِمَّا زَادَنِي شَرَفاً وَتِـيـهــا وَكِدْتُ بِأَخْمَصِي أَطَا الثريا دُخُولِي تَحْتَ قَوْلِكَ : يَعِبَادِي وَأَنْ صَيَّرْتَ أَحْمَدَ لِي نَبِيًّا قَوْلُهُ : (الذَّلِيْلُ) تَأكِيدٌ لِمَا يُفْهَمُ مِنَ العَبْدِ». قَوْلُهُ : (المُفْتَقِرْ) هُوَ أَبْلَغُ مِنَ الفَقِيرِ ) ؛ لِأَنَّ مَعْنَى المُفْتَقِرِ : شَدِيدُ الاحْتِيَاجِ، وَمَعْنَى الفَقِيرِ» المُحْتَاجُ ، لا لأَنَّ بِنَاءَ المُفْتَقِرِ» زَائِدٌ عَلَى بِنَاءِ الفَقِيرِ»؛ لِأَنَّ مَحَلَّ قَوْلِهِمْ: زِيَادَةُ البِنَاءِ تَدُلُّ عَلَى زِيَادَةِ المَعْنَى إِذَا اتَّحَدَ نَوْعُ الكَلِمَتَيْنِ ؛ كَأَنْ يَكُونَا اسْمَيْ فَاعِلٍ، أَوْ صِفَةٌ مُشَبَّهَةٌ، وَمَا هُنَا لَيْسَ كَذَلِكَ ؛ لِأَنَّ المُفْتَقِرَ اسْمُ فَاعِلِ يَدُلُّ عَلَى الحُدُوثِ ، وَالفَقِيرَ صِفَةٌ مُشَبَّهَةٌ تَدُلُّ عَلَى الدَّوَامِ . نَعَمْ يُمْكِنُ أَنْ يُجْعَلَ المُفْتَقِرُ) صِفَةٌ مُشَبَّهَةٌ بِأَنْ يُرَادَ مِنْهُ الدَّوَامَ . . قَوْلُهُ : (لِرَحْمَةِ المَوْلَى أَيْ : لإِحْسَانِهِ أَوْ لِإِرَادَتِهِ ؛ لِأَنَّهُ لَا يَصِحُ إِرَادَةُ المَعْنَى الأَصْلِي فِي حَقِّهِ تَعَالَى، وَهُوَ : «الرِّقَةُ» ؛ لِاسْتِحَالَتِهِ عَلَيْهِ تَعَالَى، وَإِذَا اسْتَحَالَ إِطْلَاقُهَا فِي حَقِّهِ تَعَالَى بِاعْتِبَارِ مَبْدَئِهَا ، جَازَ إِطْلَاقُهَا فِي حَقِّهِ تَعَالَى بِاعْتِبَارِ غَايَتِهَا وَهِيَ الإِحْسَانِ، أَوْ إِرَادَتِهِ؛ وَهِيَ عَلَى الْأَوَّلِ : صِفَةُ فِعْلٍ، وَعَلَى الثَّانِي : صِفَةُ ذَاتٍ . وَ المَوْلَى يُطْلَقُ عَلَى مَعَانٍ كَثِيرَةٍ مِنْهَا : الحَلِيفُ ، وَالنَّاصِرُ ، وَالحَلِيمُ الَّذِي لَا يَسْتَفِرُّهُ الغَضَبُ . قَوْلُهُ : (العَظِيْمِ) أَيْ : عَظَمَةٌ مَعْنَوِيَّةٌ، لَا حِرِّيَّةٌ؛ لِاسْتِحَالَتِهِ عَلَيْهِ تَعَالَى، فَإِنَّهَا تَسْتَدْعِي الجِسْمِيَّةَ. قَوْلُهُ : (المُقْتَدِرْ) هُوَ أَبْلَغُ مِنَ القَادِرِ » ؛ لِأَنَّ مَعْنَى المُقْتَدِرِ »: تَامُ القُدْرَةِ، وَمَعْنَى القَادِرِ» : المُتَّصِفُ بِالقُدْرَةِ، وَيَصِحُ هُنَا أَنْ يُقَالَ : لِأَنَّ زِيَادَةَ البِنَاءِ تَدُلُّ عَلَى زِيَادَةِ المَعْنَى؛ لاتِّحَادِ نَوْعِ الكَلِمَتَيْنِ المَذْكُورَتَيْنِ، فَإِنَّهُمَا اسْمَا فَاعِلِ. قَوْلُهُ : (الأَخْضَرِيُّ) نِسْبَةٌ لِـ «الأَخْضَر جَبَلْ بِالمَغْرِبِ عَلَى مَا قَالَهُ بَعْضُ المَغَارِبَةِ. وَهَذَا بَيَانُ لِنِسْبَتِهِ بِحَسَبِ مَا اشْتُهِرَ عَلَى الأَلْسِنَةِ، وَإِلَّا فَهُوَ مَنْسُوبٌ لِلعَبَّاسِ بْنِ مِرْدَاسَ الصَّحَابِيِّ المَشْهُورِ، كَمَا قَالَهُ المُصَنِّفُ فِي شَرْحِهِ. قَوْلُهُ : (عَابِدُ الرَّحْمَنِ) إِنَّمَا زَادَ الأَلِفَ فِي ذَلِكَ لِلوَزْنِ، وَإِلَّا فَاسْمُهُ: «عَبْدُ الرَّحْمَنِ»، وَيُحْتَمَلُ أَنَّ المُصَنِّفَ لَمْ يُرِدِ العَلَمَ . قَوْلُهُ : (المُرْتَجِيْ أَي : المُؤَمِّلَ مَعَ الأَخْذِ فِي الأَسْبَابِ كَمَا يُعْلَمُ مِمَّا مَرَّ، وَمَعْمُولُ قَوْلِهِ : المُرْتَجِيْ مَا ذَكَرَهُ بِقَوْلِهِ : «مَغْفِرَةٌ تُحِيطُ ... إلخ » ، وَقَوْلِهِ : وَإِنْ يُبَنَا ... إلخ». قَوْلُهُ : ( مِنْ رَبِّهِ المَنَّانِ) أَيْ : كَثِيرِ المَنِّ ؛ الَّذِي هُوَ الإِنْعَامِ، أَوْ تَعْدَادُ النِّعَمِ ، وَهُوَ بِالمَعْنَى الثَّانِي مَذْمُومٌ ؛ إِلَّا بِالنِّسْبَةِ اللهِ وَرَسُولِهِ ، وَاسْتَتَنى بَعْضُهُمُ الشَّيْخَ وَالوَالِدَ . قَوْلُهُ : (مَغْفِرَةٌ) مَأخوذَةٌ مِنَ الغَفْرِ (۳) وَهُوَ : السِّتْرُ، وَالمُرَادُ بِهَا : سِتْرُ الذُّنُوبِ عَنْ أَعْيُنِ المَلَائِكَةِ قِيلَ : مَعَ كَوْنِهَا بَاقِيَةٌ فِي الصَّحِيفَةِ، لَكِنْ لَا يُؤَاخِذُ بِهَا صَاحِبُهَا، وَقِيلَ: مَعَ مَحْوِهَا مِنَ الصَّحِيفَةِ مِنْ أَصْلِهَا . قَوْلُهُ : (تُحِيْطُ بالذُّنُوبِ كِنَايَةٌ عَنْ كَوْنِهَا تَعُمُّ جَمِيعَهَا بِحَيْثُ لَا يَبْقَى فَرْدٌ مِنْهَا .
And his statement (the servant): meaning the one characterized by servitude which is the utmost humility and submission, and this description is the noblest and highest of human descriptions because of what it contains of indication of the perfection of God Most High and the need of others for Him due to its indication of complete humility and submission to the Master, blessed and exalted. For this reason, the Messenger of God, may God bless him and grant him peace, was described with it in the highest stations: like the station of the Night Journey, the station of the revelation of the Qur'an, and the station of calling to Him. God Most High said: 'Exalted is He who took His servant by night' [Al-Isra: 1], 'Praise be to God who sent down upon His servant the Book' [Al-Kahf: 1], 'And that when the servant of God stood calling upon Him' [Al-Jinn: 19], and others. Then he, peace be upon him, was given the choice between being a prophet-king and a prophet-servant, and he chose the second. And among what is attributed to Qadi 'Iyad: [in the meter al-wafir]: 'And what increased my honor and pride, so that I almost step on the Pleiades with the sole of my foot, is my entering under Your saying: O My servants, and that You made Ahmad a prophet for me.' His statement (the lowly) is a confirmation of what is understood from 'the servant.' His statement (the in need) is more intensive than 'the poor' because the meaning of 'al-muftaqir' is intensely needy, and the meaning of 'al-faqir' is needy, not because the pattern of 'al-muftaqir' is longer than the pattern of 'al-faqir', because the place of their saying 'increase in pattern indicates increase in meaning' is when the type of the two words is the same, like both being active participles or descriptive adjectives, and here it is not so, because 'al-muftaqir' is an active participle indicating temporality, and 'al-faqir' is a descriptive adjective indicating permanence. Yes, it is possible to make 'al-muftaqir' a descriptive adjective by intending from it permanence. His statement (for the mercy of the Master) meaning: for His beneficence or for His will, because it is not valid to intend the original meaning with respect to Him Most High, which is 'tenderness' because of its impossibility upon Him Most High. And when it is impossible to apply it to Him Most High in terms of its origin, it is permissible to apply it to Him Most High in terms of its outcome, which is beneficence, or His will. And it is, according to the first, an attribute of action, and according to the second, an attribute of essence. And 'al-mawla' is applied to many meanings, among them: ally, supporter, and the forbearing one whom anger does not arouse. His statement (the Great) meaning: a conceptual greatness, not physical, because of its impossibility upon Him Most High, for it entails corporeality. His statement (the Powerful) is more intensive than 'the powerful one', because the meaning of 'al-muqtadir' is perfect in power, and the meaning of 'al-qadir' is the one described with power. And it is valid here to say: because increase in pattern indicates increase in meaning, because the type of the two mentioned words is the same, for they are both active participles. His statement (al-Akhdari) is a relative attribution to 'al-Akhdar', a mountain in the Maghreb according to what some Maghrebis said. And this is an explanation of his lineage according to what is commonly known by tongues; otherwise, he is attributed to al-'Abbas ibn Mirdas, the famous companion, as the author said in his commentary. His statement (worshipper of al-Rahman) He added the alif only for the meter; otherwise his name is 'Abd al-Rahman, and it is possible that the author did not intend the proper noun. His statement (the one who hopes) meaning: the one who expects while taking the means, as is known from what has passed. And the object of his statement 'the one who hopes' is what he mentioned by his statement 'a forgiveness that encompasses... etc.' and his statement 'and if we are built... etc.' His statement (from His Lord, the Bestower) meaning: abundant in bestowal, which is granting favors, or counting favors. And it is, in the second sense, blameworthy except with respect to God and His Messenger, and some excluded the teacher and the father. His statement (forgiveness) is derived from 'al-ghafr' which is concealment, and what is intended by it is the concealment of sins from the eyes of the angels. It is said: while they remain in the record, but their owner is not taken to task for them; and it is said: with their erasure from the record entirely. His statement (encompasses the sins) is a metaphor for it encompassing all of them such that no individual sin remains.
Source pages p. 354

Commentary
This passage is a commentary by al-Bajuri on the opening lines of the poem 'al-Sullam al-Murawnaq' by al-Akhdari. The author explains the meaning of the poet's self-description as 'the servant, the lowly, the in need of the mercy of the Master, the Great, the Powerful.' He begins by extolling the description 'servant' ('abd), stating it is the noblest human attribute because it acknowledges God's perfection and human need. He supports this with Qur'anic verses where the Prophet is called 'abd in the Night Journey, the revelation of the Qur'an, and his call. He then mentions that the Prophet chose to be a prophet-servant over a prophet-king, and cites a poetic line by Qadi 'Iyad about the honor of being a servant. Next, he clarifies that 'al-dhalil' (lowly) reinforces the meaning of 'abd. He then distinguishes between 'al-muftaqir' and 'al-faqir', noting that 'muftaqir' is more intense and temporally rooted, while 'faqir' is a permanent state. He adds that it is possible to interpret 'muftaqir' as permanent if desired. Then he explains 'rahmat al-mawla' as either God's beneficence (an attribute of action) or His will (an attribute of essence), since 'mercy' in its literal sense of tenderness cannot apply to God. He lists some meanings of 'mawla': ally, supporter, forbearing. He then notes that 'al-'azim' (the Great) refers to conceptual, not physical, greatness, and that 'al-muqtadir' (the Powerful) is more intensive than 'al-qadir' because of the increased pattern and both are active participles. After explaining these divine attributes, he turns to the poet's name. He states that 'al-Akhdari' is an attribution to a mountain called al-Akhdar in the Maghreb, but actually the poet traces his lineage to al-'Abbas ibn Mirdas, a famous Companion, as the author himself mentioned in his commentary. He then notes that the poet's name 'Abid al-Rahman' is actually 'Abd al-Rahman' but the alif was added for meter; it may not be a proper noun. He explains 'al-murtaiji' as one who hopes while taking means. He then clarifies 'al-Mannan' (the Bestower) as abundant in giving favors, but warns that counting favors is blameworthy except by God and His Messenger (and, some say, by a teacher or parent). Finally, he defines 'maghfirah' (forgiveness) as concealment of sins from angels, with two opinions: sins remain but are not punished, or they are erased entirely. And 'tuhitu bi al-dhunub' (encompasses sins) is a metaphor for complete coverage, leaving no sin unencompassed.

Key Terms
الأخضري
المنان
المغفرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentary, what is the real lineage of the poet al-Akhdari?

B) He is attributed to al-'Abbas ibn Mirdas, a Companion.
C) He is from the tribe of Quraysh.
D) He is a descendant of the Prophet.

Key Takeaway
The poet's lineage and the divine attributes al-Mannan and maghfirah require careful interpretation to avoid error and preserve theological correctness.

Grammatical Analysis of 'لا سيما' (Especially)
Author explains two usages of 'لا سيما' with grammatical analysis.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the two usages of 'لا سيما' (followed by noun vs. prepositional phrase) and identify its grammatical function as an indicator of priority.

Core Idea
'لا سيما' prioritizes what follows, but its grammar changes depending on what follows it.

This passage from al-Bajuri's commentary on al-Bannani unpacks the grammar of 'لا سيما', showing that it is not a fixed expression but has two distinct constructions. Understanding this helps you read classical Arabic texts with precision, especially in legal and theological arguments where 'لا سيما' signals a priority claim.

Guided Path
1
Identify the function of 'لا سيما'
The passage states that 'لا سيما' indicates priority (أولوية) of what follows over what precedes in the ruling. This is the core semantic purpose.
2
Distinguish the two constructions
Look at the examples: one with a noun (زيد) and one with a prepositional phrase (على الفرس). Notice how the meaning shifts: in the first case it means 'no one like Zaid', in the second it means 'especially on the horse'.
3
Analyze the grammatical parsing
When a noun follows, 'لا سيما' is analyzed as 'لا مثل الذي هو زيد' (there is no like the one who is Zaid). When a prepositional phrase follows, it is interpreted as 'خصوصاً' (specifically) in the accusative as an absolute object for an implied verb.
4
Note the interpolative waw
The waw prefixed to 'لا سيما' in some cases is اعتراضية (extra/interpolative) and does not affect the meaning. This is an important grammatical note attributed to al-Radi.
5
Relate to the overall passage
Understand that this is an expansion (probe) of the matn's text by the commentator, clarifying the grammar. The passage uses examples from everyday language to illustrate the rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اعْلَمْ أَنَّ هَذَا التَّرْكِيبَ يُسْتَعْمَلُ لِيُفِيدَ أَوَّلَوِيَّةَ مَا بَعْدَهُ مِمَّا قَبْلَهُ فِي الحُكْمِ، لَكِنْ: - تَارَةً يُذْكَرُ بَعْدَهُ اسْمٌ ؛ نَحْوُ : جَاءَنِي القَوْمُ لَا سِيَّمَا زَيْدٌ، وَالمَعْنَى حِينَئِذٍ : لَا مِثْلَ الَّذِي هُوَ زَيْدٌ مَوْجُودٌ بَيْنَ القَوْمِ الَّذِينَ جَاؤُني ، بَلْ هُوَ الأَخَصُّ مِنْهُمْ بِالمَجِيء إِلَيَّ. - وَتَارَةٌ يُذْكَرُ بَعْدَهُ جَارٌ وَمَجْرُورٌ مَثَلاً ؛ نَحْوُ : أُحِبُّ زَيْداً لا سِيَّمَا عَلَى الفَرَسِ، وَالمَعْنَى حِينَئِذٍ : خُصُوصاً عَلَى الفَرَسِ ؛ أَي وَأَخَصُّهُ بِزِيَادَةِ المُحَبَّةِ خُصُوصاً عَلَى الفَرَسِ، فَلَا سِيَّمَا بِمَعْنَى خُصُوصاً فِي مَحَلِّ نَصْبٍ عَلَى أَنَّهُ مَفْعُولٌ مُطْلَقٌ لِفِعْلٍ مُقَدَّرٍ ، وَالوَاوُ الدَّاخِلَةُ عَلَيْهَا فِي بَعْضِ عَلَى كُلِّ مِنَ الحَالَتَيْنِ المَذْكُورَتَيْنِ اعْتِرَاضِيَّةٌ، أَفَادَهُ الرَّضِيُّ مُلَخَّصاً.
Know that this construction is used to indicate the priority of what comes after over what comes before in the ruling. However: sometimes a noun is mentioned after it, e.g., 'The people came to me, especially Zaid.' The meaning then is: 'There is no one like Zaid among the people who came to me, but he is the most specific among them in coming to me.' And sometimes a prepositional phrase is mentioned after it, e.g., 'I love Zaid, especially on the horse.' The meaning then is: 'Specifically on the horse,' meaning 'and the most specific among them in increased love is especially on the horse.' So 'لا سيما' is in the meaning of 'specifically' in the accusative case as an absolute object for an implied verb. The waw that enters it in some cases in both mentioned situations is interpolative. Al-Radi summarized this.
Source pages p. 359

Commentary
This passage is a grammatical and semantic explanation of the phrase 'لا سيما' (especially). It begins by stating that this construction is used to give priority to what follows over what precedes in a ruling. Then it elaborates two distinct usages. The first is when a noun appears after 'لا سيما', as in the example 'جاءني القوم لا سيما زيد' (The people came to me, especially Zaid). The meaning here is that Zaid is the most specific or outstanding among those who came; there is no one like him. The second usage is when a prepositional phrase follows, as in 'أحب زيداً لا سيما على الفرس' (I love Zaid, especially on the horse). Here, 'لا سيما' takes the meaning of 'خصوصاً' (specifically) and is in the accusative case as an absolute object for an implied verb. The author notes that the waw (و) sometimes prefixed to 'لا سيما' in both constructions is extra (interpolative) and does not affect the meaning. This explanation is attributed to Radi al-Din al-Astarabadi, a well-known grammarian. The passage demonstrates a close reading of the matn's wording, clarifying its linguistic precision.

Key Terms
لا سيما
أولوية
اعتراضية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the meaning of 'لا سيما' when followed by a prepositional phrase, according to the passage?
A) بقدر (as much as)
B) خصوصاً (specifically)
C) مع (with)
D) لأجل (for the sake of)

Key Takeaway
The phrase 'لا سيما' has two grammatical constructions: one with a noun following, meaning 'there is no one like', and one with a prepositional phrase, meaning 'especially' and functioning as an absolute object.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Identify the type of 'لا سيما' (followed by noun or prepositional phrase) in these sentences and explain the grammatical analysis according to the passage: (a) جاء العلماء لا سيما الشيخ. (b) أحب طلاب العلم لا سيما في المسجد.
?
Find an instance of 'لا سيما' in a Qur'anic verse or hadith and determine its function and grammatical state based on the two usages described.

Defining 'Qarn' and the Method of Lexical Clarification
Author defines 'قرن' and explains the matn's description of the tenth century.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to compare the two definitions of 'قرن' and identify the author's intended meaning in the context of the matn.

Core Idea
The term 'قرن' is debated: a moderate period vs. exactly 100 years.

In this lesson, we examine how the commentator clarifies the term 'قرن' (century) in the matn phrase 'في عاشر القرون'. He presents two definitions, evaluates them, and identifies the author's choice. This exemplifies the lexical analysis essential in Islamic sciences for accurate understanding of texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term being defined
Locate the word 'قرن' in the Arabic text. It appears in the plural 'القرون' and is the subject of the commentator's clarification.
The term occurs in the phrase 'في عاشر القرون'.
2
Extract the two definitions
Note the two opinions presented: (a) a moderate amount of time, and (b) one hundred years. The commentator explicitly states that the first is 'the most balanced and best' (أعدل الأقوال وأحسنها), but the second is the intended meaning of the author (مُرَادُ المُصَنِّفِ).
The first definition is based on the general sense of moderation; the second is a precise numerical value.
3
Understand the commentator's role
The commentator provides both definitions, ranks them, and then specifies the author's intent. This shows his method: presenting the scholarly range, then narrowing to the context.
4
Apply this to other terms in the passage
Notice how the commentator similarly defines 'جهل', 'فساد', and 'فُتون' by giving concise lexical explanations. This consistent method demonstrates the importance of defining key terms before interpretation.
For 'جهل', he gives the famous bipartite division: simple (lack of knowledge) and compound (false belief).
5
Reflect on the rhetorical conclusion
The passage ends with a rhetorical exclamation and supplication, which depends on the correct understanding of the tenth century's description. This shows how lexical clarity underpins doctrinal and moral lessons.

قَوْلُهُ : (فِي عَاشِرِ القُرُونِ) أَيْ : مِنَ الهِجْرَةِ النَّبَوِيَّةِ عَلَى صَاحِبِهَا أَفْضَلُ الصَّلَاةِ وَأَزْكَى التَّحِيَةِ، وَلَا يَخْفَى أَنَّ القُرُونَ جَمْعُ: «قَرْنِ»، وَقَدِ اخْتُلِفَ فِيهِ عَلَى أَقْوَالٍ كَثِيرَةٍ : - مِنْهَا : أَنَّهُ اسْمٌ لِقَدْرٍ مُعْتَدِلٍ مِنَ الزَّمَنِ ، وَهُوَ أَعْدَلُ الأَقْوَالِ وَأَحْسَنُهَا . - وَمِنْهَا : أَنَّهُ اسْمٌ لِمِئَةِ سَنَّةٍ ، وَهُوَ مُرَادُ المُصَنِّفِ، كَمَا ذَكَرَهُ فِي شَرْحِهِ » (١) . قَوْلُهُ : ذِي الجَهْلِ أَيْ : ذِي أَهْلِ الجَهْلِ ؛ بَسِيطاً كَانَ وَهُوَ : عَدَمُ العِلْمِ بِالشَّيْء»، أَوْ مُرَكَّباً وَهُوَ : اعْتِقَادُ الشَّيْءِ عَلَى خِلَافٍ مَا هُوَ عَلَيْهِ . وَقَوْلُهُ : (وَالفَسَادِ) أَي : الخُرُوجِ عَنِ الحَالَةِ المُسْتَقِيمَةِ . وَقَوْلُهُ : (وَالفُتُونِ) جَمْعُ: «فِتْنَةِ»، وَهِيَ : «الشَّرُّ الَّذِي يُفْتَتَنُ بِهِ». وَإِذَا كَانَ هَذَا حَالُ القَرْنِ العَاشِرِ ، فَمَا بَالُكَ بِمَا بَعْدَهُ مِنَ القُرُونِ الَّتِي انْتَشَرَتْ فِيهَا الفِتَنُ، وَكَثُرَتْ فِيهَا المِحَنُ ، وَذَهَبَتْ فِيهَا العُلَمَاءُ الأَعْلَامُ، وَظَهَرَتِ الجُهَلَاءُ اللَّقَامُ، نَسْأَلُ اللهَ تَعَالَى أَنْ يُوفِّقَنَا لِمَا يُرْضِيهِ عَلَى الدَّوَامِ بِجَاءِ سَيّدِنَا مُحَمَّدٍ خَيْرِ الأَنَامِ، وَآلِهِ وَصَحْبِهِ الغُرِّ الكِرَامِ .
His statement: 'in the tenth of the centuries' means from the Prophetic hijra, upon its owner be the best prayers and purest greetings. And it is not hidden that 'قرون' is plural of 'قرن'. There are many opinions about it: among them that it is a name for a moderate amount of time, which is the most balanced and best opinion. And among them that it is a name for one hundred years, which is the intention of the author, as he mentioned in his commentary. His statement: 'possessor of ignorance' means possessor of people of ignorance; simple ignorance which is lack of knowledge of a thing, or compound ignorance which is belief of something contrary to what it is. His statement: 'and corruption' means departure from the correct state. His statement: 'and trials' plural of 'فتنة' which is the evil by which one is tried. And if this is the state of the tenth century, what do you think of the centuries after it in which tribulations spread, calamities increased, great scholars departed, and ignorant ones appeared... We ask Allah to guide us to what pleases Him always, by the prestige of our master Muhammad, the best of mankind, and his family and companions.
Source pages p. 359

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn's phrase 'في عاشر القرون ذي الجهل والفساد والفتون' (in the tenth century, possessing ignorance, corruption, and trials). It first clarifies that 'القرون' refers to centuries from the Hijra. Then it explains that the word 'قرن' (century) has multiple definitions: some say it is a moderate period of time (the best opinion), while others say it is exactly one hundred years—the latter being the author's intended meaning. Next, it defines the three adjectives describing the tenth century: 'جهل' (ignorance) is divided into simple (absence of knowledge) and compound (false belief); 'فساد' (corruption) means deviation from the correct state; and 'فتون' (trials) is the plural of 'فتنة' (evil that tests people). The passage then rhetorically emphasizes that if the tenth century was like this, later centuries are even worse, with more trials, loss of scholars, and rise of ignorant people. It concludes with a supplication for guidance and praise upon the Prophet. This illustrates the commentator's method of lexical and conceptual clarification.

قرن
جهل
فساد
فتنة

Key Takeaway
The commentator distinguishes between two definitions of 'قرن' and identifies the author's intended meaning as one hundred years, demonstrating the importance of lexical clarity in Islamic texts.

Decoding the Composition Date and Key Terms
Author explains the date and details of the poem's composition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine the composition date of a classical text from its internal phrasing and explain the key terms used in the dating.

Core Idea
The composition date of al-Bannani's poem is hidden in a puzzle of case endings and substitute phrases.

Authors often embed the date of composition in their works. This passage shows how al-Bajuri deciphers al-Bannani's phrasing to pinpoint the exact year and century. Understanding the linguistic clues and the reasoning behind the date helps you see how scholars handled historical information.

Guided Path
1
Identify the date phrases
Locate the phrases that indicate the date: 'في أوائل المحرم' (in the beginning of Muharram), 'من سنة إحدى وأربعين' (from the year one and forty), and 'من بعد تسعة من المئين' (after nine from the hundreds). These together give the year.
2
Parse the grammatical roles
Notice that 'مِنْ سَنَةٍ' is a circumstantial qualifier (ḥāl) for 'الأوائل' or 'المحرم'. 'إحدى وأربعين' is a substitute (badal) or clarification. This grammatical analysis ensures the correct attachment of the year to the month.
3
Resolve the numeric reading
The year is not explicitly 'nine hundred and forty-one' but given as 'one and forty after nine from the hundreds'. Understand that 'تسعة من المئين' means 900 (nine hundreds), so 'one and forty' (41) after that gives 941. Note the subtlety about whether it refers to the end of the year 940 or 'one and forty' itself.
The commentator notes that if 'إحدى وأربعين' is a substitute, it must refer to the end of the fortieth year, unless the whole-from-part substitution is accepted.
4
Determine the century
Based on the rule that a century (qarn) is 100 years, the year 941 falls in the 10th century AH. The text states: 'فهو في عاشر القرون' (so it is in the tenth of centuries). This matches the author's own statement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَوْلُهُ : (وَكَانَ فِي أَوَائِلِ المُحَرَّمِ) أَيْ: فِي الأَزْمِنَةِ الَّتِي هِيَ أَوَائِلُ المُحَرَّمِ، وَإِنَّمَا سُمِّيَ الشَّهْرُ المَعْرُوفُ بـ (المُحَرَّمِ»؛ لِتَحْرِيمِ القِتَالِ فِيهِ فِي صَدْرِ الإِسْلَامِ. وَقَوْلُهُ : (تَألِيْفُ ... إلخ) فَاعِلُ «كَانَ»؛ بِنَاءً عَلَى أَنَّهَا تَامَّةٌ كَمَا هُوَ المُتَبَادَرُ ، وَمَعْنَى التَّألِيفِ»: ضَمُّ شَيْءٍ إِلَى شَيْءٍ عَلَى وَجْهِ فِيهِ أُلْفَةٌ» - بِضَمِّ الهَمْزَةِ .. وَمُرَادُهُ بِـ الرَّجَزِ» : المَنْظُومُ مِنْ بَحْرِ الرَّجَزِ الَّذِي أَجْزَاؤُهُ مُسْتَفْعِلُنْ سِتَّ مَرَّاتٍ، وَلَعَلَّ المُرَادَ بـ «المُنَظَّمِ : تَامُّ النِّظَامِ ، لَا المَنْظُومُ، وَإِلَّا لَمْ يَكُنْ لَهُ فَائِدَةٌ بَعْدَ قَوْلِهِ : هَذَا الرَّجَزِ»، فَلْيُتَأَمَّلْ وَلِيُرَاجَعْ. قَوْلُهُ : (مِنْ) سَنَةٍ : إِحْدَى وَأَرْبَعِيْنَ) أَيْ : حَالَ كَوْنِ أَوَائِلِ المُحَرَّمِ مِنْ سَنَةِ ... إلخ، أَوْ حَالَ كَوْنِ : : المُحَرَّمِ مِنْ سَنَةِ ... إلخ، فَقَوْلُهُ: «مِنْ سَنَةٍ ... إلخ » حَالٌ مِنَ الأَوَائِلِ»، أَوْ مِنَ المُحَرَّمِ»، وَقَوْلُهُ : إِحْدَى وَأَرْبَعِيْنَ، بَدَل أَوْ عَطْفُ بَيَانِ ، لَكِنْ لَا بُدَّ أَنْ يُرَادَ آخِرُ سِنِي إِحْدَى وَأَرْبَعِيْنَ حَتَّى يَصُحُ ذَلِكَ. نَعَمْ؛ عَلَى القَوْلِ بِإِثْبَاتِ بَدَلِ الكُلِّ مِنَ الْبَعْضِ لَا يُحْتَاجُ إِلَى مَا ذُكِرَ . قَوْلُهُ : (مِنْ بَعْدِ نِسْعَةٍ مِنَ المِنِيْنَ أَيْ: حَالَ كَوْنِ الإِحْدَى وَالأَرْبَعِيْنَ مِنْ بَعْدِ... إلخ، فَهَذَا التَّالِيفُ كَانَ فِي المِئَةِ العَاشِرَةِ، فَهُوَ فِي عَاشِرِ القُرُونِ، كَمَا قَدَّمَهُ المُصَنِّفُ؛ بِنَاءً عَلَى القَوْلِ بأَنَّ «القَرْنَ» اسْمٌ لِمِئَةِ سَنَةٍ كَمَا مَرَّ .
His statement: 'and it was in the beginning of Muharram' means in the times which are the beginnings of Muharram. The month known as Muharram is so named because of the prohibition of fighting in it at the beginning of Islam. His statement: 'the composition...' is the subject of 'كان', based on it being complete (tamma). The meaning of 'تأليف' is bringing a thing together with another thing in a way that has familiarity (ulfa). What he means by 'رجز' is the poem composed in the meter of rajaz whose feet are 'mustaf'ilun' six times. Perhaps what is meant by 'المنظم' is 'complete in order' not 'composed', otherwise there would be no benefit after saying 'this rajaz'. Let it be pondered and reviewed. His statement: 'from the year one and forty' means while the beginning of Muharram is from the year... etc. So his statement 'from the year...' is a circumstantial qualifier of 'الأوائل' or 'المحرم', and his statement 'one and forty' is a substitution or clarification, but it must be intended the end of the years of one and forty for that to be valid. Yes, according to the view that permits substitution of the whole from the part, there is no need for what was mentioned. His statement: 'after nine from the thousands' means while the one and forty is after... So this composition was in the tenth century, as the author presented, based on the opinion that 'قرن' is a name for one hundred years, as passed.
Source pages p. 360

Commentary
This passage provides the date of composition of the poem (the matn) and analyzes its terminology. It begins by explaining 'أوائل المحرم' (the beginnings of Muharram) and the reason for the month's name (because fighting was prohibited in it at the dawn of Islam). It then treats the word 'تأليف' (composition) as the subject of the verb 'كان' in the sense of existence, defining 'تأليف' as combining things in a harmonious manner. The term 'رجز' is defined as a poem in the rajaz meter, whose foot is 'mustaf'ilun' repeated six times. There is a subtle point: the commentator suggests that 'المنظم' (the organized) might here mean 'complete in order' rather than merely 'composed' to avoid redundancy after saying 'هذا الرجز' (this rajaz). Then follows a grammatical parsing of the date phrase: 'مِنْ سَنَةٍ إِحْدَى وَأَرْبَعِيْنَ' (from the year one and forty). The commentator explains that 'مِنْ سَنَةٍ' is a circumstantial qualifier (ḥāl) and that 'إِحْدَى وَأَرْبَعِيْنَ' is a substitute (badal) or clarification. He notes that to be precise, it should refer to the end of the fortieth year, unless one adopts the view that the whole can be substituted from a part. Finally, 'مِنْ بَعْدِ تِسْعَةٍ مِنَ المِئِينَ' (after nine from the hundreds) indicates that the year is 941 AH, placing the composition in the 10th century (since 941 falls in the 10th century according to the 100-year definition). This lesson is a good example of how commentators combine historical, lexical, and grammatical analysis.

Key Terms
تأليف
رجز
محرم

A) The first century AH
B) The tenth century AH
C) The eleventh century AH
D) The ninth century AH

Key Takeaway
The composition date 941 AH can be derived by combining the phrases 'إحدى وأربعين' (41) and 'تسعة من المئين' (900) with careful attention to grammatical roles.
